67 (676)
A╠Дdityas
Matsya S─Бmmada or M─Бnya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi or many fish caught in a net [bahavo matsy─Б j─Бlanaddh─Бс╕е]
21 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
According to the Anukramaс╣З─л, a fish (Matsya) or тАЬmany fish caught in a netтАЭ are two of the three possible composers of this hymn. Unfortunately, there is not a scrap of evidence in the hymn itself for these intriguing ascriptions. The poet begs the ─Аdityas and their mother Aditi, who is more prominent in the hymn than in most ─Аditya hymns (vss. 10тАУ12, 14, 18), for shelter and protection from a range of dangers and enemies and for continued life for ourselves and our progeny.

Jamison Brereton Notes

─Аdityas

English translation:

тАЬ─Аdityas, hasten to us before our death, while we are yet alive; where are you, hearers of prayer?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Where are you: kat, ke = who; kva (Nirukta 6.27)

Jamison Brereton

Gird us, alive, against the deadly blow, o ─Аdityas.
Are you ones who heed the call?

A predicative voc. in a question.

English translation:

тАЬGreat, O deities, is (the guild) of the sinner, but to the sinless is happiness; ─Аdityas, you are void ofsin.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O gods, does there exist wide (space emerging) from out of constraint? Does there exist a treasure for the blameless man,
o ─Аdityas, you (whom othersтАЩ) offenses cannot mislead?

Jamison Brereton Notes

├бdbhutainasaс╕е is generally taken as a gen. sg., parallel to ├бn─Бgasaс╕е in b.

But since the only other ex. of this stem modifies the Maruts in V.87.7, I think it likely that it is a nom. pl. modifying the ─Аdityas. Moreover there is no NOM + ├бsti construction in c as there are in a and b. There is perhaps too much machinery in the tr., to indicate that it is not the ─АdityasтАЩ offenses, but those of others, that cannot deceive or mislead them (=the gods), but given the ─АdityasтАЩ character, I think the internal structure of the cmpd would be clear to the audience.

English translation:

тАЬLet not the snare bind us; may Indra, the renowned, the subduer of all, deliver us for a glorious act.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let this fetter here not bind us; let it avoid us for our great (good fortune?),
for only Indra is famous for imposing his will.

Jamison Brereton Notes

What to supply with mah├й is somewhat up in the air, but some equivalent of GeldnerтАЩs тАЬGl├╝ckтАЭ seems harmless enough.

I donтАЩt understand IndraтАЩs role here. Is the idea that Varuс╣Зa & Co. should not be getting any ideas about tying us up, because only Indra gets to do such things? But this would run counter to Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs role, at least in later Vedic, of binding offenders.

In any case the theme of binding recurs in this hymn; cf. vss. 14, 18.

Griffith

Let not this fetter bind us fast: may he release us for success;
For strong is Indra and renowned.

English translation:

тАЬO deities, ready to protect, move us not with the destructive net of our wicked enemieс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abhipramс╣Ыkс╣гata: from mс╣Ыj instrumental ad of mс╣Ыс╣г: let us not (be tormented) by the destructive net of our enemies,deliver us from it.

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt (harm) us with the harm of crooked cheats.
O gods greedy to help, seize them!

Jamison Brereton Notes

In ab I supply a transitive form of тИЪmс╣Ыc тАШharmтАЩ to be construed with the cognate instr. root noun. The fact that the verb of p─Бda c, (abh├н pr├б) mс╣Ыkс╣гata, though derived from тИЪmс╣Ы┼Ы тАШtouchтАЩ, could technically be an s-formation to тИЪmс╣Ыc makes the generation of a verb from that root easier, and in fact we might consider mс╣Ыkс╣гata as representing both тАШharmтАЩ and тАШseizeтАЩ. Oldenberg notes the phonological play.

In its other two occurrences aviс╣гy├║- has the negative sense тАШgreedyтАЩ and is clearly related to avas├б- тАШfoodтАЩ, etc. (see EWA s.v. avas├б-), but here it must be positive. I assume a portmanteau pun, combining тАШgreedyтАЩ with an association with тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ, resulting in тАШgreedy[=eager] to helpтАЩ.

Griffith

O Gods who fain would lend your aid, destroy not us as ye destroy
Your enemies who go astray.

Nicht packt uns, die ihr gerne helft, o G├╢tter, durch Besch├дd’gung an der Feinde, die voll T├╝cke sind.

English translation:

тАЬWide-traversing, far-reaching goddess, put forth your power to come to us, innocent ones, that ourchildren may live.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Make faultless (shelter) for us, o widely spreading (goddess) possessing a wide enclosure, (for us) to extend afar
and for our offspring to live.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since aneh├бs- is an adjective, a noun needs to be supplied with it (contra Geldner, Renou). I supply тАШshelterтАЩ on the basis of VIII.18.21 (also a hymn to the ─Аdityas) containing aneh├бс╕е тАж triv├бr┼лtham тАж chard├нс╕е, with the v├бr┼лtha- and chard├нs- found in our vss. 3b, 6b.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The doubling of 1st pl. pronouns, naс╕е тАж asm├бt can be interpr. in two different ways. On the one hand, naс╕е can be just a Wackernagel-position placeholder, doubled by the more emphatic (and case-marked) asm├бt later in the vs. Of course enclitic naс╕е is not technically supposed to represent an ablative, but I think that all bets are off with Wackernagel-position pronominal enclitics. Or the naс╕е can actually be an accusative, construed with ├бjaghnuс╣г─л.

English translation:

тАЬ─Аdityas and Aditi, let that which releases us as a prisoner from his bond, be ever the object of ourpraise and worship.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

That which releases us: either the net or your favour; the net itself is supposed be thefavour of the gods to become as it were the instrumental ument of deliverance

Jamison Brereton

This is the new (life) for an older (man) that will free us, o ─Аdityas, like a bound man from his bondage, o Aditi.

English translation:

тАЬLet not this weapon of Vivasvat, this net made with hands, ─Аdityas, destroy us before old age.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vivasvat: i.e. Yama, son of Vivasvat; before old age: pur─Б = p┼лrve nu id─Бn─лm sarvadetyarthaс╕е jarasahid─Бn─лm j─лrс╣З─Бn: let it not destroy us, now and of old infirm

Jamison Brereton

O ─Аdityas, let the missile of Vivasvant, the finely made arrow,
not strike us now before old age.

Griffith

Let not Vivasvan’s weapon nor the shaft, Adityas, wrought with skill,
Destroy us ere old age be nigh.

Geldner

Nicht soll uns das Gescho├Я des Vivasvat, die kunstvolle Waffe, ihr Aditis├╢hne, noch vor dem Alter t├╢ten.

Grassmann

Nicht m├╢ge des Vivasvat Spiess, Aditja’s, sein gespitzter Pfeil, Uns treffen, eh’ wir Greise sind.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

Jamison Brereton

O ─Аdityas, rip apart hostility, apart constraint, apart what is packed together;
rip malady apart and asunder.
